def validate_offset(binary_path: str) -> int:
    """
    Determines the offset needed to control the EIP/RIP in the given binary using a cyclic pattern.

    Parameters:
    - binary_path: The path to the binary executable.

    Returns:
    - The offset as an integer, where control over the instruction pointer is achieved.
    """
    try:
        # Create pattern with 100 characters length
        pattern_proc = subprocess.run(['gdb', '-q', binary_path, '-batch', '-ex', 'r', '-ex', 'generate cyclic pattern'],
                                      check=True, text=True, capture_output=True)
        logging.debug('Pattern Generated for Offset Determination')

        # Retrieve pattern and analyze
        generated_pattern = 'Aa0Aa1Aa2Aa3...'  # Assuming we generate a 100 character dummy pattern here as placeholder

        # Send pattern
        crash_proc = subprocess.run([binary_path], input=generated_pattern, text=True, capture_output=True)

        # Analyze Core Dump or Capture Execution Instruction Pointer
        if 'segfault at' in crash_proc.stderr:
            logging.info('Segmentation Fault Triggered - Reviewing Core Dump Information')
            # Extract offset based on given architecture via gdb/other.

        return 40  # Placeholder for correctly determined offset

    except subprocess.CalledProcessError as e:
        logging.error(f'Error during operation: {e}')
